      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16773979401106754994">Dor agreed to act as King of Xanth so long as Trent was gone for a week. But the weeks passed and Trent did not return. Dor knew he had to rescue his king but with no magic powers, how could it be done...?</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1834796?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 30, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely" class="user" title="J.G. Keely">J.G. Keely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/442128.Centaur_Aisle" title="Paperback 9780345352460" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=childhood" class="actionLinkLite">childhood</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=novel" class="actionLinkLite">novel</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=america" class="actionLinkLite">america</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1834796">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer755590720839686619">The first Piers Anthony book I ever read.<br /><br />At my middle school, there was a yearly book drive where everyone would bring in boxes of books from home and all the kids could go buy books for a dollar. I would always buy anything that had a dragon or a knight on the cover. That's how I got into Piers, Dragonlance, Eddings, and all that other Junior High stuff. Not to mention Conan.<br /><br />I got this book there, and needless to say, as an eleven-year-old, Anthony was hilarious. Especially in these early books</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText755590720839686619">The first Piers Anthony book I ever read.<br /><br />At my middle school, there was a yearly book drive where everyone would bring in boxes of books from home and all the kids could go buy books for a dollar. I would always buy anything that had a dragon or a knight on the cover. That's how I got into Piers, Dragonlance, Eddings, and all that other Junior High stuff. Not to mention Conan.<br /><br />I got this book there, and needless to say, as an eleven-year-old, Anthony was hilarious. Especially in these early books, which had not yet become the endless list of fan-suggested puns and ephebophilic anti-sexuality that are his current fare. His early works are fairly amusing and harmless; even his penchant for escapism is toned down considerably.<br /><br />Of course, looking back upon him, one cannot but blanch at his stilted prose, Mary Sue protagonists, puerile humor, and even more puerile sexuality. I know he does have some adult fans, and truthfully, I'm glad they're inside reading the latest Xanth novel instead of out in the world somewhere, voting.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://starsbeetlesandfools.blogspot.com/2012/06/suggested-readings-in-fantasy.html">My Fantasy Book Suggestions</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="755590720839686619">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer87872247">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17726107518240500780">This was my favorite Xanth book by far. This book more than any other figured preeminently into altering who I was as a young man. Young love, sexual tension, heroism, principles and danger; it was really all I wanted after I read this book.<br /><br />Even if I go back and discover these books weren't as good as I remember (highly likely considering the span of years that's passed), I gotta give credit to them for helping raise me in a sense. Senses of justice were pretty much instilled in me by these book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17726107518240500780">This was my favorite Xanth book by far. This book more than any other figured preeminently into altering who I was as a young man. Young love, sexual tension, heroism, principles and danger; it was really all I wanted after I read this book.<br /><br />Even if I go back and discover these books weren't as good as I remember (highly likely considering the span of years that's passed), I gotta give credit to them for helping raise me in a sense. Senses of justice were pretty much instilled in me by these books, like new-age Arthurian legends. <br /><br />A teacher of mine said that we don't really have any modern fairy tales or fables, especially none that serve the same purpose of teaching a lesson (i.e., red-riding hood and the danger of strangers) but these books did just that for me. I wanna give you a hug Anthony (even if you are a corpse) for helping instill something in me at a young age. I can't think of a better collection of books to give to a young reader. Just fantastic.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17726107518240500780">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2384324260160639294">This book started out really slow! But in the end I loved it, and can't wait to read the 5th. I really don't know why people say these books are so sexist because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Irene proposes to Dor <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and also what Dor thought of at that time (and I quote) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ "She had a body, true--but what pleased him most was the loyalty implied.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText2384324260160639294">This book started out really slow! But in the end I loved it, and can't wait to read the 5th. I really don't know why people say these books are so sexist because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Irene proposes to Dor <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and also what Dor thought of at that time (and I quote) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ "She had a body, true--but what pleased him most was the loyalty implied. She is useful.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ There is ALSO the fact that Irene instigates the whole sexual portion of the relationship.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>She is a women and a real person, not written in a sexist way. <span id="freeTextContainer10692258611242966551">Another really fun adventure in Xanth. Dor is the second generation to be chronicled and this is his second adventure. King Trent is raising Dor in the palace to give him training in how to be a monarch. However, this got interrupted when King Trent went on a week's visit to Mundania and never came back. This isn't great literature I suppose,</span>

Dor and several companions including the king's daugher, Irene, set out to find the King and rescue him. The puns flow quickly in this romp. As does love. This isn't great literature I suppose, but what a fun ride it is!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1401666676">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1401666676" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2254872-matt" class="left imgcol" title="Matt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1406094901p2/2254872.jpg" alt="Matt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1401666676?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2254872-matt" class="user" title="Matt">Matt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96980.Centaur_Aisle" title="Paperback 9780345418524" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1401666676">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17242629190933827949">A friend gave me this book. I was traveling and gave it a shot, because I hadn't tried any other books by Piers Anthony.<br /><br />So, it's better than most magazines. It's not Terry Pratchett entertaining, but it was (barely) entertaining enough that I finished the book. A couple times, I almost stopped, but did finish it. The book contains some stereotypes of women that I found pretty sexist, but might also be the sort of mild titillation that could get a teenager interested in reading more.<br /><br />I will say th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17242629190933827949">A friend gave me this book. I was traveling and gave it a shot, because I hadn't tried any other books by Piers Anthony.<br /><br />So, it's better than most magazines. It's not Terry Pratchett entertaining, but it was (barely) entertaining enough that I finished the book. A couple times, I almost stopped, but did finish it. The book contains some stereotypes of women that I found pretty sexist, but might also be the sort of mild titillation that could get a teenager interested in reading more.<br /><br />I will say that if you're a fan of this series, you'll probably enjoy the book just fine. And Piers Anthony does a fairly good job of taking his universe's rules and tweaking them a bit, then examining the consequences.<br /><br />If you're looking for funny or pun-related fantasy novels, I'd start with Terry Pratchett. If you're looking for serious fantasy novels, I'd start with The Name of the Wind. If you're looking for self-aware fantasy novels that play with the crossover between our world and a fantasy world--and you've already read the Chronicles of Narnia--then you might try Wizard's Bane, about a computer programmer who is transported into a fantasy world.<br /><br />Maybe I'm being a bit too negative. If I ran across another Piers Anthony book, I'd probably be pretty happy to read it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17242629190933827949">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1006236587">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10181907542865593850">Dor is entrusted with holding down the throne while Magician Trent is away in Mundania--land of no magic!--but when Trent doesn't return, he has to go find out why. However, he and his helpers have very little power to rescue anyone if they can't use their magical talents, and since magic doesn't work outside Xanth, they've got to find a way to get around it. Good thing the centaur Arnolde--whose magical talent is creating a magic aisle in places where there is no magic--is there to pave their w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10181907542865593850">Dor is entrusted with holding down the throne while Magician Trent is away in Mundania--land of no magic!--but when Trent doesn't return, he has to go find out why. However, he and his helpers have very little power to rescue anyone if they can't use their magical talents, and since magic doesn't work outside Xanth, they've got to find a way to get around it. Good thing the centaur Arnolde--whose magical talent is creating a magic aisle in places where there is no magic--is there to pave their way!<br /><br />This one disappointed me because I would have liked to see what people who depend on magic do when their greatest strength is removed. I also found the idea that all centaurs hate magic kind of unlikely. Why would one race all collectively hate something that's integral to the world they live in? Just seemed like a simplistic way to get Arnolde banished from his kind, since centaurs aren't supposed to have magical talents. It was also disappointing how externally guided this quest was. There's always a specific goal and a single answer for everything.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer975778558">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8203581352096588542">I must disclose that I really enjoy the Xanth series. I love relaxing with some brain candy during the weekend, simply enjoying the story. So I rated the book 4 stars, when if possible, I would have given it 3 1/2 stars.<br /><br />This is the fourth book in the Xanth Series. Dor is now 16, and King Trent has him running the kingdom while he has gone to Mundania to try to meet with a country to establish a trading partner. It was supposed to last only a week. Then it becomes longer and longer, and King Tren</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8203581352096588542">I must disclose that I really enjoy the Xanth series. I love relaxing with some brain candy during the weekend, simply enjoying the story. So I rated the book 4 stars, when if possible, I would have given it 3 1/2 stars.<br /><br />This is the fourth book in the Xanth Series. Dor is now 16, and King Trent has him running the kingdom while he has gone to Mundania to try to meet with a country to establish a trading partner. It was supposed to last only a week. Then it becomes longer and longer, and King Trent and Queen Iris have not returned.<br /><br />Getting help from Irene, Smash, Grundy and Chet they start out on an adventure to find King Trent, and along the way discover the new Magician that has suddenly appeared in the land of Xanth. Whether Dor is able to complete his journey will help determine if he can rule a kingdom, while along the way trying to figure out his true feelings for Irene.<br /><br />It is a fun adventure, one that is the first to have the characters have a prolonged exposure to Mundania, and one that starts to show how Xanth is land of puns. This book is a solid edition to the continuation of the Xanth series. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_925112221">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/925112221" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3921570-ryk-stanton" class="left imgcol" title="Ryk Stanton"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1277434942p2/3921570.jpg" alt="Ryk Stanton" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/925112221?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3921570-ryk-stanton" class="user" title="Ryk Stanton">Ryk Stanton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96980.Centaur_Aisle" title="Paperback 9780345418524" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer925112221">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12486254693005250772">I'm working my way through the Xanth series and finding it quite enjoyable. There's a bit of nostalgia – these were the gateway books that led me into a life of loving fantasy novels, and I still read them with quite a bit of fondness. Reading it as an old man and as a much more seasoned reader than I was when I first read these books as a teenager (that long ago? really?), I might under some circumstances be forced to critique these books as somewhat ham-handed and contrived – one of the reason</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12486254693005250772">I'm working my way through the Xanth series and finding it quite enjoyable. There's a bit of nostalgia – these were the gateway books that led me into a life of loving fantasy novels, and I still read them with quite a bit of fondness. Reading it as an old man and as a much more seasoned reader than I was when I first read these books as a teenager (that long ago? really?), I might under some circumstances be forced to critique these books as somewhat ham-handed and contrived – one of the reasons I stopped reading Xanth was that I became aware of how formulaic they were – but these early novels especially have a great sense of fun and sweetness to them that makes me feel very forgiving.<br /><br />If you haven't read this series, then I really recommend you pick up the first book (A Spell for Chameleon) and fall in love with Xanth.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12486254693005250772">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/1215378.Centaur_Aisle" title=" 9780708881064" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tweens who liked the Harry Potter Books</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to David by: </span>
      Stewart Wymer

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer253501972">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1775832054628527517"><strong>A trip to Mundania to rescue a king</strong><br />30 December 2011<br /><br /> One of the things that I noticed about the Xanth Series is that while they were written in a particular order, and while it is probably helpful to read them in order, it is probably not necessary to do so. Personally, even though the books do not directly follow on from each other, as do most trilogies or series, it is hinted that the books are following a vague time line. Obviously Centaur Aisle follows on after Castle Roogna, but not directly</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1775832054628527517"><strong>A trip to Mundania to rescue a king</strong><br />30 December 2011<br /><br />	One of the things that I noticed about the Xanth Series is that while they were written in a particular order, and while it is probably helpful to read them in order, it is probably not necessary to do so. Personally, even though the books do not directly follow on from each other, as do most trilogies or series, it is hinted that the books are following a vague time line. Obviously Centaur Aisle follows on after Castle Roogna, but not directly.<br />	King Trent decides to go on a journey and puts Dor in charge of the kingdom. However Trent does not return when he is supposed to and Dor brings some friends together (a Golem and an Ogre, I think, it has been a long time since I read this book, so I am grateful to Wikipedia for having summaries of pretty much every one). Trent has gone to Mundania to try to establish trade routes, but he is captured. The catch with Mundania is that magic does not work there, so Dor and his friends travel to an island and meet up with a cantaur (Centaurs hate magic) who has been exiled because of a gift. His gift is the ability to create a field of magic where there is none. So armed with this 'weapon' they travel to Mundania to rescue King Trent.<br />	It should be noted that Dor's gift is the ability to communicate with inanimate objects, which is a very useful gift for a king to have. The thing with Xanth is that everybody has a gift, but it is not like atypical fantasy novels where magic is learnt through hard study and is possessed by a few. Magic in Xanth is a birthright, however all one gets is that one gift, so it comes down to how this gift is used.<br />	Some have suggested that these books are about hope, struggle against impossible odds, and never giving up. Sure, it is a common thread through a lot of books, but I would hardly say that it is worthy of writing an essay on. Even then, by year 12 my English Teacher would hardly have been impressed with me writing an essay on a Xanth Novel, when in his mind there are plenty of better novels out there on which one can write an essay.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1775832054628527517">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/100276015?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 13, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1420737-john" class="user" title="John">John</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/906179.Centaur_Aisle" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345318084" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1420737-john?shelf=xanth" class="actionLinkLite">xanth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer100276015">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12627956923529446527">This is the fourth book in the series and the second of Dor's adventures. With a group of friends (previous characters or children of previous characters) he sets off on a quest to find a danger threatening the land of Xanth. <br /><br />The characters are interesting and the group works well together as a team. Every character is given something important to do, and each of them has an opportunity to demonstrate their own unique talents. I cannot recall any part of the book where a character might have bee</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12627956923529446527">This is the fourth book in the series and the second of Dor's adventures. With a group of friends (previous characters or children of previous characters) he sets off on a quest to find a danger threatening the land of Xanth. <br /><br />The characters are interesting and the group works well together as a team. Every character is given something important to do, and each of them has an opportunity to demonstrate their own unique talents. I cannot recall any part of the book where a character might have been "forgotten" during the story.<br /><br />More of the world of Xanth is revealed to us, in particular "Centaur Isle", the home of the Centaurs. They are amongst the most important citizens of the realm, in the form of teachers or scholars or other supportive roles, offering guidance and wisdom to the human rulers of Xanth. Their history and origin are also revealed, which is somewhat disturbing, but interesting nonetheless.<br /><br />The author does a fine job of allowing us to visualize the land of Xanth, and I found my imagination inspired by the vivid descriptions present. The trademark humor of the series is still there, and I found myself laughing out loud on more than one occasion. There are of course more puns, which a reader may or may not appreciate. It is clearly something to expect from the series now.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I have one minor issue with this book. "Centaur Aisle" does not offer insight into the current lives of Bink or Chameleon, and never really delves into what is happening in their lives. This is my biggest disappointment in the book. While the author does make references to those characters, and events in previous books, the focus is purely on Dor for the most part. King Trent plays an important role in the book, and it is good to at least have him present. I simply would have thought it better if there was some interaction between Dor and his parents. It would have made sense to do so before starting this epic quest. Regardless, the book still succeeds despite this minor complaint.<br /><br />The story ends on a happy note, though there are a few lingering questions, but nothing that distracts from the overall story.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12627956923529446527">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer275893591519895892">Centaur Isle<br />A good book<br /><br />Centaur Isle<br />There is a land called Xanth where anything can happen. In Xanth everyone has magic powers.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText275893591519895892">Centaur Isle<br />A good book<br /><br />Centaur Isle<br />There is a land called Xanth where anything can happen. In Xanth everyone has magic powers. Some of the main characters are Dor, who can talk to the imamate; Irene, who can grow plants instantly; Grundy, the golem who can talk in any langue possible, and smash an ogre who has insane strength. The King of this land is king Trent. He is a very respected king. Then one day he goes missing. Dor, being second to the throne, decides to take his friends on a mission to rescue the King. There is a xanth magician whose power is knowledge. However there is a disturbance. He sensed there is a magic centaur but cannot find him. Centaurs are known for denying or not having magic.<br />This book was very hard to put down. It had a lot of Action and adventure and I surprising twist. This book is good however it’s very long so if you cant commet yourself to a long book this is not for you. The main theme of this book was never give up. Dor never gave up when he failed of did something wrong .The story was told in 3rd person I think this was a good choice so we could feel and see what all the charters a doing and thinking. This made me think, if you could have one what magical power would you have?<br /></span>

      <a href="/user/show/84660-swankivy" class="user" title="Swankivy">Swankivy</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96980.Centaur_Aisle" title="Paperback 9780345418524" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer597702247'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer597702247">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9792282854084295273">So in Xanth, centaurs hate magic. (Why a whole race would randomly hate magic is beyond me. Why a whole race would be written to all have the same opinion about something is also a rather too convenient way to create tension.) Anyway, Arnolde the centaur who has a magical talent is shunned by his kin. <br /><br />But Arnolde isn't the protagonist. Magician Dor is, once again. He's babysitting the throne while King Trent is off in Mundania, land of no magic, but something goes wrong and Trent doesn't return,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9792282854084295273">So in Xanth, centaurs hate magic. (Why a whole race would randomly hate magic is beyond me. Why a whole race would be written to all have the same opinion about something is also a rather too convenient way to create tension.) Anyway, Arnolde the centaur who has a magical talent is shunned by his kin. <br /><br />But Arnolde isn't the protagonist. Magician Dor is, once again. He's babysitting the throne while King Trent is off in Mundania, land of no magic, but something goes wrong and Trent doesn't return, so Dor takes his motley magical creature troop and tries to figure out what to do about rescuing Trent. Thing is, Dor is a little kid and the group is used to depending on their magical talents . . . which won't work when they go to Mundania. That's why they need Arnolde: his talent is creating a magic "aisle" where there is no magic. Score!<br /><br />Something that always bothered me about the Xanth books was the way they always followed from a simple solution. It was an object quest. If you find the crystal or the potion or, in this case, the magic-in-no-magic-zones centaur, you win. Someone gives you the information about what you need, and you go off looking for it (admiring the occasional female posterior and making the more than occasional pun on the way), and nobody really has to have much agency to solve the problem.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9792282854084295273">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_386368517">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/386368517" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11455886-j-austill" class="left imgcol" title="J Austill"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1369205964p2/11455886.jpg" alt="J Austill" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/386368517?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 28, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11455886-j-austill" class="user" title="J Austill">J Austill</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96980.Centaur_Aisle" title="Paperback 9780345418524" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer386368517">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9593005576788688980">What makes this book great is the Xanth formula, as mentioned in my review of A Spell for Chamelon:<br /><br />"As a general rule, Xanth novels are about a protagonist who doesn't really fit in and has no idea what their purpose in life is or what group they would fit in with. That is, they are a normal young adult. They decide to go on a Quest and over the course of said Quest they discover who they are, where they belong, and fall in love."<br /><br />This is Dor's formula and we all came to love him in the previous</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9593005576788688980">What makes this book great is the Xanth formula, as mentioned in my review of A Spell for Chamelon:<br /><br />"As a general rule, Xanth novels are about a protagonist who doesn't really fit in and has no idea what their purpose in life is or what group they would fit in with. That is, they are a normal young adult. They decide to go on a Quest and over the course of said Quest they discover who they are, where they belong, and fall in love."<br /><br />This is Dor's formula and we all came to love him in the previous book, Castle Roogna, where he set off on an adventure as a 12 year old kid. Now he's an adult and it's his turn to fall in love.<br /><br />This book has 3 plots which drive it and the strongest of those is the love story. For the first time, the female character is a real 3 dimensional female. The primary conflict occurs with the standard misunderstanding between the sexes. This story really hits home as I have certainly been that dumb guy who just didn't catch on when a girl liked him. Besides that, the likability of the two characters makes the reader root for them getting together.<br /><br />The second plot is much less interesting but is where the title comes from. Dor sets out on a quest to find a Magician level Centaur who is on his own quest to map Xanth. The flaw here was with the edition of the books that I read. The modern books all have a map of Xanth at the front and the newer the book, the more detailed the map is.<br /><br />But that is not true of the original editions (which I now own in paperback). The first 3 books have no map of Xanth and the maps slowly appears over the 4th and 5th books which share a plot of mapping Xanth. It is far less interesting to find out what Xanth looks like when you have spent 3 books looking at the map.<br /><br />The final plot is the weakest in my opinion, and I seem to recall it being the one listed on the back of the book. The King is missing and Dor has to set out on a quest to find him. This plot is almost wholly left in the background and forgotten until it is finally, and anti-climactically resolved. If it turned out that he had just been in the W.C. reading a newspaper the effect would have been the same.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9593005576788688980">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/241405-tom" class="left imgcol" title="Tom"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1344560193p2/241405.jpg" alt="Tom" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/405076631?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 01, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/241405-tom" class="user" title="Tom">Tom</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96980.Centaur_Aisle" title="Paperback 9780345418524" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer405076631">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6176441576045914007"><p>This is the fourth in a series of fantasy novels by <em>Piers Anthony</em> set in the mythical world of <strong>Xanth</strong> and stars the heir apparent to the throne, Dor. Dor is left as king of Xanth after the current ruler, <strong>Magician Trent</strong> heads to <strong>Mundania</strong> on a diplomatic mission. Dor lacks the skills to properly rule Xanth and learns some hard lessons. When Trent doesn’t return as scheduled, Dor sets off with his friends <strong>Grundy</strong>, <strong>Chet the Centaur</strong>, <strong>Smash the Ogre</strong>, and the young woman <strong>Irene</strong> in search of <em>Centaur Isle</em>.</p><p>T</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6176441576045914007"><p>This is the fourth in a series of fantasy novels by <em>Piers Anthony</em> set in the mythical world of <strong>Xanth</strong> and stars the heir apparent to the throne, Dor. Dor is left as king of Xanth after the current ruler, <strong>Magician Trent</strong> heads to <strong>Mundania</strong> on a diplomatic mission. Dor lacks the skills to properly rule Xanth and learns some hard lessons. When Trent doesn’t return as scheduled, Dor sets off with his friends <strong>Grundy</strong>, <strong>Chet the Centaur</strong>, <strong>Smash the Ogre</strong>, and the young woman <strong>Irene</strong> in search of <em>Centaur Isle</em>.</p><p>The group encounters a number of obstacles as they try to find the missing king and his wife but eventually they bring the novel to a successful conclusion.</p><p>Even as a young boy I barely made it through this novel as the plotting often makes little sense and the characters are scarcely one-dimensional. Younger boys who don’t demand much in the way of writing style might enjoy the fantasy elements of this book and the world in which it is set but I can’t recommend it to anyone.</p><p>As of September 1, 2012 there are 35 book in the series and Anthony has indicated he will continue to write them.</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9339901856504565244"><em>Dor</em>, now sixteen, is once again the main protagonist in this fourth installment. <br /><br /><strong>Centaur Aisle</strong> is my favorite book of the <em>Xanth</em> series so far. <em>Anthony’s</em> witty humor is persistent throughout and not overdone. I caught myself laughing out loud several times.<br /><br />In this volume <em>Dor</em> must work as a team with several others to attempt to rescue <em>King Trent</em> and <em>Queen Iris</em> trapped in <em>Mundania</em>.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9339901856504565244"><em>Dor</em>, now sixteen, is once again the main protagonist in this fourth installment. <br /><br /><strong>Centaur Aisle</strong> is my favorite book of the <em>Xanth</em> series so far. <em>Anthony’s</em> witty humor is persistent throughout and not overdone. I caught myself laughing out loud several times.<br /><br />In this volume <em>Dor</em> must work as a team with several others to attempt to rescue <em>King Trent</em> and <em>Queen Iris</em> trapped in <em>Mundania</em>. Several fascinating characters traveling with <em>Dor</em> each play critical roles. One traveling companion is <em>Princess Irene</em>, <em>Dor’s</em> love interest. Witnessing their relationship develop was a perfect blend of humor, romance, love, and trust. A new addition, <em>Arnolde the Centaur</em>, quickly became one of my favorite characters. <br /><br />I hope to visit <em>Xanth</em> again soon.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/157293-luke-johnson" class="left imgcol" title="Luke Johnson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1382644381p2/157293.jpg" alt="Luke Johnson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/157293-luke-johnson" class="user" title="Luke Johnson">Luke Johnson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96980.Centaur_Aisle" title="Paperback 9780345418524" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer841076758">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8174675104347826016">Seems like a more amateurish version of Terry Pratchett's Discworld, heavily targeted at the 14-year-old boy market. This is probably worth 2-1/2 stars, and the liberal and laudable use of puns pushes it to 3. It reads like an old video game or RPG, in which the characters overcome a series of unrelated obstacles in interesting ways in their journey toward their initial goal.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer834199621">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3477430055795162878">Weaker than the first three installments of the Xanth series. In this one the troupe of travelers set out on a quest (as in all of the first 8 in the series - all the one's I've read so far), but this quest seems a little more disjointed and anemic. They have a long way to go, to the very southern tip of Xanth and then back beyond its NW borders. Maybe the problem is that it was more about the travel than about accomplishing the mission.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16745800342078855049">Piers Anthony is actually quite a good author, and I would read his stuff still if it weren't for such as the occasional harpy that he throws in there. I mean, you don't see them or anything and he doesn't describe them in detail, but they are still naked on top and I just don't feel right reading a book with that imagery anymore—not that I entirely did then, either.<br /><br />I like Anthony's ability to conjure a sense of the magic of the story.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText16745800342078855049">Piers Anthony is actually quite a good author, and I would read his stuff still if it weren't for such as the occasional harpy that he throws in there. I mean, you don't see them or anything and he doesn't describe them in detail, but they are still naked on top and I just don't feel right reading a book with that imagery anymore—not that I entirely did then, either.<br /><br />I like Anthony's ability to conjure a sense of the magic of the story. There really is a lot in his books. It's maybe not the most serious style, but it still has a good strong magical feel to it.<br /><br />The characters are usually pretty cool. The puns are interesting, although I don't know that I would call them funny, exactly. They do add well to the books either way, though.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4524962672852489722">Piers Anthony's Xanth series is a comedic take on the typical fantasy novel, set in a land roughly the size and shape of Florida, where magic is real and everything is more literal. This particular book follows Dor, the heir to the throne, and Irene, his future Queen, as they attempt to find the real king and queen in Mundania (also known as "the real world"). I won't bother with plot summary because I don't think it would be very informative. The book had some very clever moments (though some p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4524962672852489722">Piers Anthony's Xanth series is a comedic take on the typical fantasy novel, set in a land roughly the size and shape of Florida, where magic is real and everything is more literal. This particular book follows Dor, the heir to the throne, and Irene, his future Queen, as they attempt to find the real king and queen in Mundania (also known as "the real world"). I won't bother with plot summary because I don't think it would be very informative. The book had some very clever moments (though some parts that were intended to be humorous came off as cheesy). I also liked the accurate depiction of the teenager's thought processes and the general style of the writing - it flows quickly from adventure to adventure.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer316647130">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17388266502380400160">In this 4th installment of the "Magic of Xanth" series, Anthony tells the story of how Dor, after being crowned regent, must locate and rescue King Trent of Xanth in his absence. <br /><br />In my opinion, this is the worst book in the series so far. Anthony makes it ABUNDANTLY clear his stance on cultural taboos like nudity and sexuality, even more-so than in the rest of the series. More pages are spent on 16-year-old Dor and 15-year-old Irene's innuendo-filled romancing and groping than on the rather unsa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17388266502380400160">In this 4th installment of the "Magic of Xanth" series, Anthony tells the story of how Dor, after being crowned regent, must locate and rescue King Trent of Xanth in his absence. <br /><br />In my opinion, this is the worst book in the series so far. Anthony makes it ABUNDANTLY clear his stance on cultural taboos like nudity and sexuality, even more-so than in the rest of the series. More pages are spent on 16-year-old Dor and 15-year-old Irene's innuendo-filled romancing and groping than on the rather unsatisfying and nonsensical climax of the story.<br /><br />That being said, Anthony's writing style still makes this book an interesting to read page turner, and I would recommend it with the rest of the series.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer865333572">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5349601261209517028">These books are great for a light read. I love the puns and the fast moving story line. The plot is cute, and I loved seeing where the story was heading. Sometimes it was predictable, but often it lead somewhere totally different than I thought it would. Although it was a bit sexist, I attribute that to the fact that it was written quite a long time ago.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17042959677507446633">It had been so long since I read this one, that I'd forgotten nearly everything, other than the barest outline. I really enjoyed how each person in the party was crucial to the success of the quest.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText17042959677507446633">It had been so long since I read this one, that I'd forgotten nearly everything, other than the barest outline. I really enjoyed how each person in the party was crucial to the success of the quest. The development of Dor and Irene's relationship was very nicely done.<br /><br />As part of this book takes place in Mundania, and Mundania is a parallel to our own world, it makes me curious about how much of the history is based upon our own timeline. I wonder what I would find if I were to delve into the history of Europe in the 8th and 9th centuries. <br /><br />Also, of note, this book includes the first of Xanth's Author's Notes. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('biwyo1g0Bn7BbM81cqTP/PxN421KnbsTwtOK5li7UFEL+A1wquYShE20u44MxSlOtbogdANA/Lmo2o90lC6mFA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8516.Piers_Anthony">About Piers Anthony</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/8516.Piers_Anthony"><img alt="8516" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1445445112p2/8516.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1858809724908628370">Though he spent the first four years of his life in England, Piers never returned to live in his country of birth after moving to Spain and immigrated to America at age six. After graduating with a B.A. from Goddard College, he married one of his fellow students and and spent fifteen years in an assortment of professions before he began writing fiction full-time.<br /><br />Piers is a self-proclaimed environm</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1858809724908628370">Though he spent the first four years of his life in England, Piers never returned to live in his country of birth after moving to Spain and immigrated to America at age six. After graduating with a B.A. from Goddard College, he married one of his fellow students and and spent fifteen years in an assortment of professions before he began writing fiction full-time.<br /><br />Piers is a self-proclaimed environmentalist and lives on a tree farm in Florida with his wife. They have two grown daughters.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/piersanthony" target="_blank">http://us.macmillan.com/author/piersa...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1858809724908628370">...more</a>
